    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="905940184e3941be93d0e30ee6618153">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '003e99e8-5286-43aa-a939-ae5b82011d80'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

        <div class="relative"><a href="#" data-db-target-for="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865" data-db-switch="icon-close_thin" aria-haspopup="true" aria-controls="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865_Pop" role="button" id="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865_Ctrl" aria-label="Tools" class="article-tools__ctrl"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Tools"></i><span>Tools</span></a><div data-db-target-of="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865" aria-labelledby="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865_Ctrl" id="0e406ce9-5c43-4e2d-b741-e0b43d1f1865_Pop" class="article-tools__block fixed dropBlock__holder"><ul role="menu" class="rlist w-slide--list"><li role="presentation" class="article-tool"><a href="https://advanced.onlinelibrary.wiley.com/action/rightsLink?doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253&amp;mode=" role="menuitem" target="_blank"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-permissions-key"></i><span>Request permission</span></a></li><li role="presentation" class="article-tool"><a href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" role="menuitem" target="_self"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-export-icon"></i><span>Export citation</span></a></li><li role="presentation" class="article-tool"><a href="/personalize/addFavoritePublication?doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" role="menuitem" target="_self"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-favorites"></i><span>Add to favorites</span></a></li><li role="presentation" class="article-tool"><a href="/action/addCitationAlert?doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" role="menuitem" target="_self"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Track-citations"></i><span>Track citation</span></a></li></ul></div></div>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en" style="">
         <h2 id="d142643938" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Metal phosphides exhibit high energy densities as hosts for lithium/sodium storage owing to their conversion reaction mechanism. Nevertheless, they typically suffer from inferior reversibility and cyclability because of the dissolution of polyphosphides and sluggish electrochemical kinetics. Herein, a series of dual-bond confined MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G composites have been fabricated, in which M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub> nanoparticles are strongly bound with MXene and graphene nanosheets via Ti─P and C-P bonds. On one hand, the dual-bond confinement offers strong adsorption to trap polyphosphides, greatly stabilizing the conversion-formed products during cycling. On the other hand, dual-bond immobilization largely promotes electron transfer and ion diffusion, facilitating the reversibility of conversion reactions. As anticipated, these MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G hybrids demonstrate superb lithium/sodium-storage performance. Particularly, as an anode for lithium-ion batteries, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G delivers a high initial coulombic efficiency of 90.1% and a high reversible capacity of 1058.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Even tested at high rates of 1.0/2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, it can still maintain high reversible capacities of 820.6/726.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 1450 cycles. When applied in pouch full-cells and sodium-ion batteries, it also shows extended cyclic lifespans of 350 and 1200 cycles. This work provides new insights to improve the reversibility and cyclability of conversion-type anodes.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202417253-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202417253-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) dominate mobile electronics, smart grids, and electric vehicles due to high energy density, extended cycle life, and environmental friendliness.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0001_R_d142643921e450" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - eScience">1</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the growing need for high energy density cannot be satisfied by commercial graphite anode with limited theoretical capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0002_R_d142643921e455" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Energy Environ. Sci.">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As an important family of conversion-type anodes, metal phosphides (MPs) possess high theoretical capacities based on the conversion reaction mechanism (M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub> + 3yLi<sup>+</sup> + 3ye<sup>−</sup> ↔ xM<sup>0</sup> + yLi<sub>3</sub>P).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0003_R_d142643921e474" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Small">3</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0004_R_d142643921e474" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Adv. Energy Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, MPs exhibit appropriate reaction potential (&lt;1.0&nbsp;V) for lithium storage, which endows with high energy densities.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0005_R_d142643921e479" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Energy Storage Mater.">5</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0006_R_d142643921e479" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Chem">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, they have also captured much interest in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), potentially replacing LIBs by virtue of the abundance and affordability of sodium reserves.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0007_R_d142643921e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Nat. Energy">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, MPs still encounter some challenges considering the overall battery performance. First, the drastic volume variation of MPs upon cycling induces structural collapse, resulting in severe capacity decay.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0008_R_d142643921e490" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - J. Mater. Chem. A">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0009_R_d142643921e490" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Energy Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Second, the inferior intrinsic conductivity of MPs triggers sluggish electrochemical kinetics, impairing the rate capability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0010_R_d142643921e495" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Energy Mater.">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0011_R_d142643921e495" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - SusMat">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> More seriously, the polyphosphide intermediates (LiP<sub>x</sub>/NaP<sub>x</sub>) formed during the conversion reaction are prone to dissolve from active material into liquid electrolyte, inevitably inducing the irreversible loss of active material and inferior reversibility of electrochemical reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0012_R_d142643921e505" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">12</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0013_R_d142643921e505" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energy Storage Mater.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Unfortunately, this phenomenon has rarely been a concern for MPs.</p>
         
         <p>To address these issues, up to now, the most effective approach is to incorporate nanostructured MPs into conductive carbon networks to form the MPs/C composites. Substantial examples, like Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-GT,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0014_R_d142643921e517" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Adv. Energy Mater.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>@CNT-C,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0015_R_d142643921e527" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - ACS Nano">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> FeP@NC,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0016_R_d142643921e532" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> CoP⊂NPPCS,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0017_R_d142643921e538" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Mater.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> CuP<sub>2</sub>/SVG,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0018_R_d142643921e545" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Chem. Eng. J.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> have been demonstrated to promote the battery performance of MPs, wherein the carbon matrices can suppress the cycle-induced volume expansion and facilitate the ion/electron transport of MPs during discharge/charge processes. Nevertheless, because of the weak van der Waals interaction between MPs particles and carbon materials, the MPs can be easily detached from substrates upon repeated cycling, which could diminish the structural stability and electrochemical kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0019_R_d142643921e550" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Chem. Eng. J.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the simple physical confinements of carbon substrates are inadequate to inhibit the dissolution of polyphosphide intermediates and volume effect upon extended cycles, which leads to fluctuating coulombic efficiency and short lifespan.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0020_R_d142643921e556" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - ACS Nano">20</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0021_R_d142643921e556" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Nano Lett.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, carbon materials with limited capacities could inevitably sacrifice the energy densities of MPs/C composites, hindering their development in electric vehicles and smart grids.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0022_R_d142643921e561" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Adv. Energy Mater.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> MXene, a type of 2D metal carbide, has received much attention for energy applications by virtue of its exceptional electrical conductivity, low ion diffusion barrier, and high mechanical flexibility.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0023_R_d142643921e572" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The unique physicochemical properties of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> MXene make it an ideal substrate for anchoring active particles to construct composites for rechargeable batteries.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0024_R_d142643921e582" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Nano Energy">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For example, Yin et al<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0025_R_d142643921e587" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Adv. Energy Mater.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> fabricated Si/MXene composites as anodes for LIBs via a low-temperature reduction strategy, where the MXene sheets not only acted as conductive channels for Li<sup>+</sup> transfer but also relieved the cycled-induced volume change of Si. Li et al<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0026_R_d142643921e595" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Nano-Micro Lett.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> used the phosphorene/MXene heterostructure to construct an asymmetric membrane electrode via a self-assembly strategy, which exhibited improved electrochemical stability and kinetics for LIBs. Noteworthily, inside these hybrid composites, the Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> MXene matrix owned abundant surface redox reaction sites, which could significantly increase ion storage capacities, rather than just serve as a conductive substrate.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0027_R_d142643921e604" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>It is well known that the chemical bonding of composite matrices provides stronger coupling to active materials than physical confinement, which can ensure electrochemical stability and kinetics even after repeated cycling.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0028_R_d142643921e611" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In this context, a series of chemical bonds were successfully constructed, such as Si─O─C,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0029_R_d142643921e616" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Energy Storage Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sn─C,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0030_R_d142643921e621" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sb─C,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0031_R_d142643921e627" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> P─C,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0032_R_d142643921e632" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Nano Lett.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Fe─N─C,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0033_R_d142643921e638" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> etc., which significantly improved the battery performance. As for the MPs anodes, researchers have demonstrated that the P─C/P─O─C bonds constructed between CuP<sub>2</sub>/Fe<sub>2</sub>P species and carbon matrices can greatly promote the buffer effect on volume expansion and particle agglomeration of active materials during cycling.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0019_R_d142643921e647" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Chem. Eng. J.">19</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0034_R_d142643921e647" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Chem. Commun.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the dissolution of polyphosphides for MPs has not been well addressed by the sole chemical bond. Thus, it is crucial to employ rational chemical bonds to fabricate well-interacting composites, greatly enhancing the electrochemical reversibility and stability.</p>
         
         <p>Inspired by these facts, we utilize Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> MXene with high electrical conductivity and graphene nanosheets (G) with high mechanical flexibility as matrices to fabricate the dual-bond confined MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G composites. Inside the triple-phase composites, the M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub> nanoparticles are strongly bound with MXene/G through Ti─P/C─P dual bonds, as demonstrated by the theoretical calculation and experimental characterization. The dual-bond immobilization can promote the electrical conductivity and ion diffusion of MPs. Moreover, during discharge/charge processes, the dual-bond configuration offers strong chemical interaction with polyphosphide intermediates to suppress the shuttle effect of soluble polyphosphides. The much-enhanced polyphosphides adsorption and electrochemical kinetics can facilitate the back-conversion reaction of MPs, leading to high electrochemical reversibility and stability. As expected, the MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G hybrids (M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub> = Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, CuP<sub>2</sub>, FeP, and MnP) demonstrate outstanding electrochemical properties as anodes for LIBs/SIBs. Particularly, as anode for LIBs, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G composite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 960.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> after 250 cycles, with a high initial coulombic efficiency of 90.1% and high coulombic efficiencies (&gt;99.5%) after the first three cycles. Even tested at high rates of 1.0/2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, high reversible capacities of 820.6 and 726.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> can be maintained after 1450 cycles, respectively. Moreover, when used in pouch full-cells and SIBs, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G also exhibits long cyclic lifetimes of 350 and 1200 cycles. Thus, this work provides a series of high-performance MPs anodes and new insights to promote the battery performance of conversion-type anodes.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202417253-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202417253-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202417253-sec-0030">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202417253-sec-0030-title">2.1 Phase and Structure Characterization</h3>
            
            <p>The MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G hybrids were fabricated by high-energy ball milling (HEBM) in two steps. As illustrated in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1a</a>, metal powder and red phosphorus with specific molar ratios, together with 15 wt% of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> MXene were milled for 2&nbsp;h to synthesize the MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>. Then, the MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub> mixed with 15 wt% of expanded graphene (EG) were milled for 8&nbsp;h to fabricate the MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G composites. The structures of MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G were first characterized by the X-ray diffraction (XRD) technique. As revealed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1b</a>, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G hybrid reveals the typical peaks of hexagonal Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS#73-2221) without any impurities, indicating the complete phosphorization of Sn metal with compositing of MXene and carbon material. Similarly, the XRD patterns (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information) also verify the successful fabrication of MXene-CuP<sub>2</sub>-G, MXene-FeP-G, and MXene-MnP-G. In this work, we focus on the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G as representative due to its best battery performance, and the bare Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G have also been fabricated for comparison. Obviously, the peaks of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G become wider compared with the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, which implies that the introduction of MXene can suppress the particle aggregation of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> during balling synthesis. Raman spectra were characterized to further analyze the phase structure of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. As revealed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1c</a>, the peak located at 428&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> is ascribed to the characteristic mode of tin phosphide, and the peaks situated at 375 and 620&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> are ascribed to Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> MXene.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0035_R_d142643921e807" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - ACS Appl. Energ. Mater.">35</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0036_R_d142643921e807" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - ACS Nano">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G samples show obvious peaks at 1340, 1581, and 2720&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, which correspond to the D, G, and 2D bands of carbon, respectively. These bands are ascribed to the disordered carbon, ordered sp<sup>2</sup> carbon, and in-plane transverse optical phonons scattering, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0037_R_d142643921e825" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G exhibits a sharper D-band and broader G-band than the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, and its 2D-band shifts to the left, which both indicate better exfoliation of EG with the help of MXene.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417253-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/35ca8a67-9276-4972-ad86-192c316860d8/adfm202417253-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/35ca8a67-9276-4972-ad86-192c316860d8/adfm202417253-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1eab643e-3cda-462b-81d6-66c0806d8289/adfm202417253-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/35ca8a67-9276-4972-ad86-192c316860d8/adfm202417253-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417253-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic diagram of the fabrication of MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G composites. b) XRD patterns, c) Raman spectra of MXene, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. d) Sn 3d, e) P 2p, f) Ti 2p, g) C 1s XPS spectra of MXene, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. h–j) Optimized configurations of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The bonding state of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G was characterized by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS). The high-resolution Sn 3d spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1d</a>) can be fitted into two pairs of peaks at 485.2/493.6 and 486.8/495.4&nbsp;eV, which correspond to the mixed ions of Sn<sup>2+</sup> and Sn<sup>4+</sup> in Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. Remarkably, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G shows a higher Sn<sup>2+</sup>/Sn<sup>4+</sup> ratio than the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, which implies better bond coupling between MXene/G and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. In the P 2p spectrum (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1e</a>), the peaks at 127.9 and 129.1&nbsp;eV are attributed to the characteristic 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and 2p<sub>1/2</sub> of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. As seen, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> shows the existence of a P─Ti bond at 131.8&nbsp;eV, the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G shows the existence of a P─C bond at 132.8&nbsp;eV, and the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G is typical of both P─Ti and P─C bonds.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0038_R_d142643921e963" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">38</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0039_R_d142643921e963" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The P─O bond in all samples is mainly due to the inevitable oxidation of tin phosphides tested under air atmosphere.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0010_R_d142643921e969" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Energy Mater.">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0039_R_d142643921e969" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the Ti 2p spectrum (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1f</a>), apart from the characteristic peaks ascribed to Ti─C, Ti<sup>2+</sup>, and Ti<sup>4+</sup> of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> MXene, an obvious pair of peaks at 456.8/462.9&nbsp;eV occurs for the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G samples, which are due to the formation of Ti─P bond.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0038_R_d142643921e995" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Regarding the C 1s spectrum (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1g</a>), the peaks at 283.6 and 284.5&nbsp;eV belong to the sp<sup>2</sup> C═C/C─C and sp<sup>3</sup> C─C of carbon, and the peak at 281.2&nbsp;eV belong to the C─Ti of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>. Notably, the peak at 286.1&nbsp;eV appears for the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, corresponding to the formation of C─P bond.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0039_R_d142643921e1021" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The density functional theory (DFT) calculation was also performed to verify the dual-bond configuration of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. As revealed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1h,i</a>, the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G model presents obvious C─P bond with length (1.83 Å) less than the total of C and P atom radius (0.78 and 1.10 Å), the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> model shows apparent Ti─P bond (2.30 Å) with length less than the total of Ti and P atom radius (1.44 and 1.10 Å). Thus, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G model possesses a stable configuration with both C─P and Ti─P bonds (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0001">1j</a>). Additionally, the dual-bond state of MXene-CuP<sub>2</sub>-G, MXene-FeP-G, and MXene-MnP-G can also be verified by the XPS technique (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <p>The morphological structure was characterized by scanning electron microscopy (SEM) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) observations. As shown, the pristine Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> MXene exhibits a multi-layer structure, and the bare Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> presents large microsized aggregates with rough surfaces (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). In contrast, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G hybrids display a secondary microstructure made up of primary nanoparticles with smooth surface, suggesting the encapsulation of lamellar MXene or graphene sheets (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0002">2a</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). Moreover, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G presents smaller primary particles than those of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G due to the spatial confined effect of MXene during synthesis. The TEM observation in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0002">2b</a> also verifies the structure constitution of the primary nanoparticle with outside layer coating. The selected area electron diffraction (SAED) in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0002">2c</a> displays the diffraction rings due to the (012), (107), (110), (202), and (027) planes of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. The magnified TEM image (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0002">2d</a>) presents the dual-coating structure of MXene and G. The high-resolution TEM images (HRTEM) in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0002">2e,f</a> show the ultrafine nanocrystallites with lattice fringe of 0.28&nbsp;nm, corresponding to the (107) facet of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. Notably, layer structures with lattice fringes of 0.40 and 1.20&nbsp;nm are visible as outer coating, which are assigned to the few-layer graphene and MXene, respectively. In contrast, without the restriction of both FLG and FL-MXene, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> crystallites display larger sizes in bare Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information). The HAADF image and elemental mapping (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0002">2g</a>) demonstrate the homogeneous distribution of C, Ti, P, and Sn elements inside the composite structure. Thus, the above morphological observations demonstrate the successful formation of a dual-confinement structure.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417253-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/47687531-4211-4003-a96b-74085dfe6dc9/adfm202417253-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/47687531-4211-4003-a96b-74085dfe6dc9/adfm202417253-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/cb7b8531-715b-4dec-a1dd-3b926d0adc39/adfm202417253-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/47687531-4211-4003-a96b-74085dfe6dc9/adfm202417253-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417253-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) SEM image, the inset is magnified part, b) TEM image, c) SAED pattern, d) magnified TEM image, e, f) HRTEM images, g<sub>1</sub>-g<sub>5</sub>) HAADF image and element (C, Ti, P, and Sn) mapping of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G composite.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202417253-sec-0040">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202417253-sec-0040-title">2.2 Electrochemical Reversibility and Cyclic Stability</h3>
            
            <p>Cyclic voltammetry (CV) test was performed between 0.01 and 3&nbsp;V to expound the de-/lithiation processes of the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G anode, as shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0003">3a</a>. During the initial cathodic sweep, the peaks at 1.03 and 0.47&nbsp;V are attributed to the multi-step conversion reaction (Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> + 3xLi<sup>+</sup> + 3xe<sup>−</sup> → 4Sn + 3Li<sub>x</sub>P), which shift to 0.80 and 0.54&nbsp;V in the following cycles due to the activation of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0040_R_d142643921e1206" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The other reduction peaks at low potentials are assigned to the alloying of Sn (Sn + yLi<sup>+</sup> + ye<sup>−</sup> → Li<sub>y</sub>Sn).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0041_R_d142643921e1218" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Mater. Chem. A">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the inverse sweep, the peaks at 0.54 and 0.65&nbsp;V are attributed to the delithiation of Li<sub>y</sub>Sn, and the peaks at 0.82 and 1.15&nbsp;V are due to the conversion of Li<sub>3</sub>P to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0042_R_d142643921e1232" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Compared with that of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G without dual-bond confinement (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information), the CV profiles of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G exhibit great overlap after the first cycle, suggesting superior reversibility. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0003">3b</a> presents the initial discharge/charge profile of the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G electrode, it exhibits high discharge/charge capacities of 1174.6/1058.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, with an average initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) up to 90.1%. Different cells have been tested in the same conditions to verify the high ICE of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, which shows the almost same profiles and an average value of 90.1% (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information). The initial reversible capacity and ICE of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G are much higher than those of the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> (895.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, 79.5%) and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (973.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, 84.8%), mainly originating from the capacity contribution of back-conversion reaction. Notably, the ICE of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G is superior to those of other reported MPs anodes (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0003">3c</a> presents the cyclic performance tested at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, after 250 cycles, a high reversible capacity of 960.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> can be still maintained for the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, greatly superior to those of the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> (142.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (677.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). Obviously, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G exhibits higher cycling coulombic efficiencies (&gt;99.5% after the initial three cycles) than the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G samples, suggesting its superior cyclic reversibility. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0003">3d</a> shows corresponding cycling discharge/charge profiles, compared with those of the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information), the profiles of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G are almost unchanged due to the dual-bond confinement. We have also prepared composites with different contents of MXene and G (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information) to screen the optimal composition. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a> (Supporting Information), the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G composite prepared with MXene and G additions of 15 wt% and 15 wt% exhibits the best electrochemical performance. Its superior cycling performance than MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G with sole bond indicates the synergistic effect of MXene and G.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417253-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3d1f38c9-6f0f-4edd-9163-ba6e68891733/adfm202417253-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/3d1f38c9-6f0f-4edd-9163-ba6e68891733/adfm202417253-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6d7ee611-635a-4abc-9a13-753659d3487b/adfm202417253-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3d1f38c9-6f0f-4edd-9163-ba6e68891733/adfm202417253-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417253-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV profiles of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. b) Initial discharge/charge profiles and corresponding ICEs, c) cycling performance at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. d) Cycling discharge/charge profiles at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, e) rate discharge/charge profiles of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. f) Rate performance of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. g) High-rate cyclic performance of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. h) Comparison of cyclic life of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G with other MPs anodes.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0017" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0017_R_d142643921e1438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Mater.">17</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0035" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0035_R_d142643921e1438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - ACS Appl. Energ. Mater.">35</a>, <a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0040" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0040_R_d142643921e1438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">40</a>-<a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0049" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0049_R_d142643921e1438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Energy Storage Mater.">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0003">3e</a> shows the discharge/charge profiles of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G at various rates, as the rate increases, the voltage platforms show inconspicuous distortion compared with those of the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information), which indicates that Li-storage reactions are well maintained even at high rates. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0003">3f</a> reveals the superior rate performance of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, which can offer high capacity values of 783.5, 648.1, and 545.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> even at high current densities of 2.0, 5.0, and 10.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. When the rate returns to 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, it can deliver high and stable reversible capacities (&gt;1000 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) during cycling. Apparently, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G shows higher rate performance than the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, which results from the enhanced electrochemical kinetics enabled by the dual-substrate compositing. The reversibility and cyclability of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G at high rates are also revealed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0003">3g</a>, even cycled at 1.0 and 2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> for 1450 de-/lithiation cycles, it can maintain high reversible capacities of 820.6 and 726.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. The coulombic efficiencies can keep ≈99.4% during long-term cycling. Even with high mass loadings of 3.0 and 4.5&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G can still deliver a long cyclic life up to 1000 cycles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information). Notably, compared with other reported MPs anodes for LIBs, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G hybrid in this work exhibits better cyclic stability (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0003">3h</a>). Inspired by the superb performance of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, we also tested the electrochemical properties of other MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G to verify the applicability of the dual-bond confinement strategy. As shown in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18–S20</a> (Supporting Information), tested at high rate of 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the voltage profiles of MXene-CuP<sub>2</sub>-G, MXene-FeP-G, and MXene-MnP-G are well maintained during long-term cycling, and these MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G exhibit excellent reversibility and cyclability, which demonstrates that the intimate dual-bond interaction can greatly enhance the performance of MPs anodes.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202417253-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202417253-sec-0050-title">2.3 Enhanced Electrochemical Kinetics</h3>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">The electrochemical kinetics were first studied to understand the role of dual-bond configuration. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0004">4a</a> displays the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) results obtained after initially discharged at 1.5&nbsp;V, wherein the semicircular and linear components reflect the electron transport and ion diffusion processes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0015_R_d142643921e1561" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - ACS Nano">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to the equivalent circuit analysis (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information), the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G exhibits greatly reduced charge resistance (95.9 Ω) compared to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> (318.9 Ω) and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (200.3 Ω), as summarized in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information). This confirms that the dual-compositing of MXene/G can greatly improve the conductivity of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. Moreover, the correlation between Z' and ω<sup>−1/2</sup> in the low-frequency range is displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0004">4b</a>. Based on Equations <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information), the Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Li+</sub>) is inversely proportional to the Warburg factor (σ<sub>w</sub>), represented by the slope of the linear part. Obviously, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G exhibits a much lower slope (63.1) compared to the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> (380.7) and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (290.8), indicating its superior Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics. The CV curves of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G were swept from 0.2 to 1.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Supporting Information; Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0004">4c</a>), and the capacitive analysis can be performed by the Equation <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information). As revealed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information), the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G anode shows superior capacitive contributions than the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G at different rates, ranging from 56.4% at 0.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> to 79.2% at 1.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. The enhanced capacitive behavior of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G can be attributed to the supporting of MXene/G networks. The CVs can be further used to investigate the Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient based on the equation:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0050_R_d142643921e1678" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Adv. Mater.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202417253-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/ffd584f6-04bd-44bd-bbf5-bc0e030d812c/adfm202417253-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202417253:adfm202417253-math-0001" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202417253-math-0001.png">

            <div class="paragraph-element">The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) profiles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0004">4e</a>) were also tested at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> after the first 5 cycles to study the D-values based on the formula:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0015_R_d142643921e1896" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - ACS Nano">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202417253-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
