                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>where <i>m<sub>B</sub></i>, <i>V<sub>m,</sub></i> and <i>M<sub>B</sub></i> are the mass, molar volume, and mass molar of the electrode, and <i>τ</i>, <i>A</i> is the current titration time and electrode area. Δ<i>E<sub>s</sub></i> is the potential change under the current pulse, while Δ<i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> is the potential change under the galvanostatic process. As displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0004">4f</a>, the diffusion coefficients of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G range from 10<sup>−12</sup> to 10<sup>−11</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup> during discharge/charge processes, which are greater than those of the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. The superior Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics should be attributed to the dual-bond interaction of MXene/G matrices. Moreover, the diffusion energy barrier was estimated by the DFT to verify the superior de-/lithiation kinetics of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0004">4g</a> presents the Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion pathways along the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> crystal interlayers with Ti─P/C─P dual-bond and C─P sole-bond coupling. As revealed from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0004">4h</a>, the corresponding Li<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barriers of the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G model are much lower than those of the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G model, indicating the faster Li<sup>+</sup> kinetics due to the dual-bond coupling. Thus, the MPs anode with dual-bond immobilization is demonstrated with fast electrochemical kinetics, which can be beneficial for the de-alloying of Li<sub>y</sub>Sn and back-conversion of Sn/Li<sub>x</sub>P.</div>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202417253-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202417253-sec-0060-title">2.4 Improved Polyphosphide Adsorption Ability</h3>
            
            <p>To further understand the improvement mechanism of dual-bond confinement on the lithium storage reversibility, the de-/lithiation processes of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G anode were studied by in situ/ex situ analyses. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0005">5a</a> presents the in situ XRD contour plots of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G against the initial discharge/charge profile, the enhancement of peak intensity is reflected by the color variation from blue to red. Inside the plots, the peaks located at 52.8°, 50.8°, 45.6°, and 44.3° can be assigned to the Be foil and derivative BeO, respectively. During the initial discharge process, the characteristic peaks of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> are clearly observed in the plots. After discharged to 1.5&nbsp;V, these peaks gradually diminish, and the characteristic peaks of LiP<sub>5</sub> appear at 16.5°, indicating the preliminary conversion reaction of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> to LiP<sub>x</sub>. As the discharge reactions proceed, the peaks of LiP and Li<sub>3</sub>P gradually emerge, accompanied by the characteristic peaks of metallic Sn<sup>0</sup> at 30.8° and 32.7°, suggesting the deep conversion reaction to Sn<sup>0</sup> and Li<sub>3</sub>P. Then, as discharged to 0.48&nbsp;V, the Sn<sup>0</sup> peaks gradually weaken accompanied by the appearance of Li-Sn alloy peaks, resulting from the alloying reaction. The in situ XRD demonstrates the conversion reversion of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> to Li<sub>x</sub>P (LiP<sub>5</sub>/LiP/Li<sub>3</sub>P) and subsequent alloying reaction of Sn<sup>0</sup> to Li<sub>y</sub>Sn. When initially charged to 0.3&nbsp;V, the peaks of Li-Sn alloys gradually disappear with the re-formation of Sn<sup>0</sup>, which is due to the de-alloying reaction. As continuously charged to 0.8&nbsp;V, the Li-rich polyphosphide (Li<sub>3</sub>P) gradually converts to Li-poor polyphosphide (LiP and LiP<sub>5</sub>). When finally charged to 3.0&nbsp;V, both Sn<sup>0</sup> and Li<sub>x</sub>P completely vanish without phase re-generation, which can be due to the highly reversible conversion reaction to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> with low crystallinity.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417253-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/fe1880d5-44c6-4f4f-b23c-91a5f4a303af/adfm202417253-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/fe1880d5-44c6-4f4f-b23c-91a5f4a303af/adfm202417253-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/625c99a4-9682-421a-b952-0503e203811a/adfm202417253-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/fe1880d5-44c6-4f4f-b23c-91a5f4a303af/adfm202417253-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417253-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">De-/lithiation mechanism of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. a) In situ XRD contour plots against the initial discharge/charge profile. Ex situ HRTEM images and SAED patterns were observed after initially b<sub>1</sub>, b<sub>2</sub>) discharged at 0.01&nbsp;V, c<sub>1</sub>, c<sub>2</sub>) charged at 3.0&nbsp;V. d) Ex situ P 2p XPS spectra obtained after 1st discharged, 1st charged, and 250th cycled.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The ex situ TEM observations of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G anode after fully discharged and charged were conducted to further verify the above de-/lithiation processes. The HRTEM image observed after fully discharge (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0005">5b1</a>) shows the (101) plane of Li<sub>3</sub>P along with the (511) and (422) planes of Li<sub>22</sub>Sn<sub>5</sub>. The corresponding SAED pattern in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0005">5b2</a> also reveals the co-existence of Li<sub>3</sub>P and Li<sub>22</sub>Sn<sub>5</sub> products, suggesting the combined conversion and alloying reactions of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. After fully charged, ultrafine crystals (&lt; 5&nbsp;nm) with spacing of 0.28&nbsp;nm are observed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0005">5c1</a>, assigned to the (107) facet of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. The corresponding SAED pattern in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0005">5c2</a> also shows the re-formation of weak Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> phase, which confirms the complete back-conversion of Sn<sup>0</sup>/Li<sub>3</sub>P to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. The regeneration of the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> phase with low crystallinity indicates the amorphization or electrochemical grinding of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> during de-/lithation, which agrees with above in situ XRD result. Notably, the dual immobilization of MXene/G matrices can be still observed during discharge and charge processes, which ensures the high reversibility of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. The ex situ XPS analysis of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G anode was also performed to demonstrate the dual-bond confinement of MXene/G to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and lithiated derivatives during cycling. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0005">5d</a> shows the high-resolution P 2p spectra tested after initially discharged/charged and 250th cycled, apart from the 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and 2p<sub>1/2</sub> peaks, the peaks of P─Ti/P─C bonds can still be characterized in these spectra, suggesting the dual-bond immobilization of MXene/G to MPs and Li<sub>x</sub>P during cycling.</p>
            
            <p>Furthermore, ex situ analyses of cycled MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G anode at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> were conducted to verify superior cyclic reversibility. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6a</a> shows the XRD patterns of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G after fully lithiated for different cycles, the final lithiated products of Li<sub>3</sub>P and Li<sub>22</sub>Sn<sub>5</sub> are well maintained even after 10, 100, and 250 cycles. Thus, the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> phase with low crystallinity can be fully recovered for the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G after 250 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6b</a>). The ex situ Sn 3d XPS spectrum of cycled MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G shows the similarly mixed ions of Sn<sup>2+</sup> and Sn<sup>4+</sup> as a fresh electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6c</a>). By contrast, for cycled Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, the ex situ XRD spectra show obvious characteristic peaks of Sn<sup>0</sup>, and the Sn 3d XPS spectra only show metallic Sn<sup>0</sup> signal, indicating their poor reversibility of conversion reaction. To reveal the reason behind, fourier transform infrared spectroscopy (FT-IR) and UV–vis spectroscopy (UV–vis) tests were conducted on the LiPF<sub>6</sub>/EC/DEC electrolyte immersing cycled electrodes. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6d</a>, apart from the peaks of electrolyte, the new peak at 520–480&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> was detected for cycled Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G electrodes, which can be attributed to P─P bonds of polyphosphides.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417253-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417253-bib-0013_R_d142643921e2318" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energy Storage Mater.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The UV–vis spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6e</a>) also present obvious absorption of polyphosphides in the UV-band for cycled Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, and the optical images in the inset show that these electrodes become light yellow after cycling. These results imply that the dual-bond immobilization can inhibit the dissolution of polyphosphides during cycling, which leads to the high reversibility of the conversion reaction. The TEM observation of cycled MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G electrode was also conducted to verify the reversible conversion of Sn<sup>0</sup>/Li<sub>3</sub>P to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6f</a>, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G still displays a transparent nanostructure, in which the supporting of MXene/G can be still observed, and the SAED pattern reveals the complete resumption of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>. The HRTEM image (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6g</a>) exhibits the structure of ultrafine Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> crystals (≈5&nbsp;nm) tightly connected with MXene/G matrices. The element mapping further illustrates the even distribution of P, Sn, Ti, and C elements (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6h</a>). The mass ratio of Sn to P elements can be estimated to be 5.36 after cycling, which approaches the theoretical ratio (5.12) for fresh Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6i</a>). For comparison, the cycled Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G presents obvious particle agglomeration, and the corresponding SAED pattern and HRTEM image reveal the formation of Sn<sup>0</sup> grains (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25a–c</a>, Supporting Information). The EDS mapping also shows the phenomenon of Sn coarsening, and the mass ratio of Sn to P was calculated as high as 12.96 (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a>, Supporting Information), which is due to the dissolution of polyphosphides.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417253-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7ab51bae-e3b6-466f-85f0-2ca2a361e6dd/adfm202417253-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/7ab51bae-e3b6-466f-85f0-2ca2a361e6dd/adfm202417253-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6d9695b2-4650-4a00-9b56-9d0125f6d7ed/adfm202417253-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7ab51bae-e3b6-466f-85f0-2ca2a361e6dd/adfm202417253-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417253-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G after fully lithiated for different cycles. b, c) XRD patterns and XPS spectra of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G after 250 cycles. d) FT-IR spectra, e) UV–vis spectra of electrolytes immersing cycled Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, and MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G electrodes, the inset is the optical graphs of electrodes. f) TEM image, the inset is SAED pattern, g) HRTEM image, h) elemental mapping, i) EDS analysis of cycled MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. j) Adsorption energies of MXene/G and G to lithium polyphosphides with dual-bond and sole-bond. k) Schematic graph of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G anode upon de-/lithiation processes.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The DFT calculation was further conducted to demonstrate the strong adsorption effects of dual-bond (Ti─P/C─P) confinement to the lithium polyphosphides (Li<sub>x</sub>P). Here, LiP<sub>7</sub>, LiP<sub>5</sub>, LiP<sub>3</sub>, LiP, and Li<sub>3</sub>P were selected as polyphosphide species to construct the structure models of MXene-Li<sub>x</sub>P-G with dual-bond link and Li<sub>x</sub>P-G with sole-bond link, as listed in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information). Consequently, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6j</a>, the adsorption energies of MXene/G to LiP<sub>7</sub>, LiP<sub>5</sub>, LiP<sub>3</sub>, LiP, and Li<sub>3</sub>P species with dual-bond immobilization can be calculated as −6.95, −6.23, −10.91, −9.69, and −10.82&nbsp;eV, respectively, which are much higher than those of G to corresponding polyphosphides (−5.27, −4.76, −5.99, −8.01, and −6.17&nbsp;eV) with sole-bond confinement. The high chemical adsorption effect of the dual-bond structure can effectively prevent the dissolution of Li<sub>x</sub>P intermediates, thus enhancing the reversibility of M<sup>0</sup>/Li<sub>3</sub>P to MPs. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0006">6k</a> illustrates the enhancement mechanism behind the excellent reversibility and cyclability of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G. On the one hand, the Ti─P/C─P dual-bond connection of MXene/G shows high adsorption energies to Li<sub>x</sub>P species, which can greatly suppress the dissolution of polyphosphides to electrolytes and stabilize the lithiation-formed products. On the other hand, the dual-immobilization of conductive MXene/G matrices can largely promote the de-/lithiation kinetics, thus facilitating the reversibility of Sn<sup>0</sup>/Li<sub>3</sub>P to Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202417253-sec-0070">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202417253-sec-0070-title">2.5 Electrochemical Performance of Pouch Full-Cells and SIBs</h3>
            
            <p>To further evaluate the application value of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G anode, the pouch full-cells were assembled by using the LiFePO<sub>4</sub> cathode, which owns high capacity output and long cyclic life (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information). The specific capacity and energy density were estimated based on the total mass of the anode and cathode. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0007">7a</a> shows the galvanostatic charge/discharge curves of pouch full-cells tested at 0.2 C (1 C = 130&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>), they exhibit a high discharge capacity of 93.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and two obvious discharge plateaus of 2.86/2.45&nbsp;V. The corresponding energy density can reach up to 285.6&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>, which can easily light up the LED lamp. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0007">7b</a> presents the cycling performances along with CEs of full-cells, they can still retain high reversible capacities of 73.5/54.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.5/2.0 C even after 350 cycles, with CEs surpassing 99.3% after the first 5 cycles. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0007">7c</a> shows the inconspicuous variation in the cyclic charge/discharge curves at 0.5 C, which implies the stable electrochemical structure of full cells. The charge/discharge curves at various rates are also depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0007">7d</a>, the voltage platforms have been well maintained even at high rates of 2.0/5.0 C. Accordingly, the full-cells can still deliver high reversible capacities of 59.6/49.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> even at 2.0/5.0 C, respectively, with capacity ratios of 66.2%/57.8% relative to that at 0.2 C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0007">7e</a>). The energy/power densities of full-cells are also summarized, they&nbsp;can still obtain high energy densities of 140.8/97.5&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> as the power density rises to 3.26/5.63&nbsp;kW kg<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a>, Supporting Information). Notably, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G//LiFePO<sub>4</sub> full-cells exhibits superior cycling and rate performances to most of the reported full cells (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417253-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/aab9f0b4-6fab-4552-bc93-0b9bc4b80b1a/adfm202417253-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/aab9f0b4-6fab-4552-bc93-0b9bc4b80b1a/adfm202417253-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/22fc6ffe-58e8-4cf8-a328-22752210891f/adfm202417253-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/aab9f0b4-6fab-4552-bc93-0b9bc4b80b1a/adfm202417253-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417253-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417253" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of pouch full-cells. a) Charge/discharge profiles tested at 0.2 C for the first 5 cycles, the inset is the image of LED powered by pouch full-cells, b) cycling performances along with CEs at 0.5 C and 2.0 C, c) cycling charge/discharge profiles at 0.5 C, d, e) rate charge/discharge profiles and rate performance. Na-storage performance. f) Cycling discharge/charge profiles of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, the inset is the schematic diagram, g, h) rate capability and high-rate cyclic capability of MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Moreover, we also investigated the electrochemical performance of MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G for sodium storage. The corresponding mechanism of conversion and alloying reactions was elucidated by CV curves and differential capacity plots, which are described thoroughly in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a> (Supporting Information). The galvanostatic test (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0007">7f</a>) shows that the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G delivers high initial discharge/charge capacities of 686.5/601.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, with a high ICE of 87.7%. Remarkable cyclic stability with a well-maintained voltage platform and specific capacity has also been achieved for the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G, which outperforms those of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32</a>, Supporting Information). When tested at high rates of 2, 5, and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G can deliver high capacities of 394.9, 321.2, and 265.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, which are much higher than those of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0007">7g</a>, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S33</a>, Supporting Information). Even tested at 1.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> for 1200 cycles, high capacity up to 435.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> can be still retained for the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417253-fig-0007">7h</a>). The full-cells were further assembled using Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as the cathode to explore the application potential for SIBs, which can deliver a high reversible capacity of 83.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, a long life of 150 cycles, and high rate capability (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S34</a>, Supporting Information). Hence, the dual-bond configuration can endow the Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> anode with fast and stable sodium storage. Moreover, the high-rate capability and long cyclic life are also achieved in the MXene-CuP<sub>2</sub>-G, MXene-FeP-G, and MXene-MnP-G anodes for SIBs, which successfully validate the applicability of this strategy.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202417253-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202417253-sec-0080-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>To conclude, we have deeply studied the phase transitions of MPs upon de-/lithiation and revealed the key issue of polyphosphides dissolution for unsatisfied reversibility and cyclability. Furthermore, we have successfully fabricated a series of dual-bond confined MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G composites, which display the architecture of M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub> nanoparticles strongly bound with MXene/G matrices through Ti─P/C─P bonds. As demonstrated by in situ/ex situ characterizations, electrochemical analysis, and DFT calculation, the dual-bond immobilization not only offers strong adsorption effect to polyphosphide species but also enables fast electrochemical kinetics, thus greatly facilitating the reversibility of conversion reaction. As expected, these MXene-M<sub>x</sub>P<sub>y</sub>-G composites demonstrate superb reversibility and cyclability as anodes for LIBs/SIBs. In particular, the MXene-Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>-G representative delivers a high ICE/capacity output (90.1%/1058.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> for LIBs, 87.7%/601.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> for SIBs), ultralong lifespan (1450 cycles for LIBs, 1200 cycles for SIBs), and high-rate capability. Thus, this strategy can also be extended to other conversion-type anodes for high-performance LIBs/SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202417253-sec-0090-title"> Acknowledgements</h2>
